### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 78 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A newspaper costs $4 on Sunday and $1 the rest of the days of the week. If a hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week and pays $210 per week for newspapers, how many newspapers does it buy on Monday?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 30
  C: 45
  D: 60
  E: 75
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's start with the cost of the newspaper per week.
  The hotel buys two times as many newspapers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week.
  If the hotel buys x newspapers on a regular day, it buys 2x newspapers on Sunday.
  Therefore, the total number of newspapers the hotel buys in a week is 6x (one Sunday and six other days).
  The cost of the newspaper on Sunday is $4 and the cost of the newspaper on other days is $1.
  The total cost of the newspapers per week is $210.
  So, we can set up an equation: 4(2x) + 1(6x) = 210
  Solving for x, we get x = 15.
  Therefore, the hotel buys 15 newspapers on a regular day and 30 newspapers on Sunday.
  The hotel buys 90 newspapers in total (15 newspapers/day * 6 days + 30 newspapers on Sunday).
  To find out how many newspapers the hotel buys on Monday, we subtract 30 (newspapers bought on Sunday) from 90 (total newspapers bought) and divide by 6 (number of days other than Sunday): (90 - 30)/6 = 10
  Therefore, the hotel buys 10 newspapers on Monday.
  The answer is A: 15. 
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let's call the number of newspapers the hotel orders on Monday "x".
We know the hotel orders twice as many newspapers on Sunday as it does on Monday, so it orders 2x newspapers on Sunday.
The hotel orders 7 newspapers in a week (one for each day).
So, the hotel orders 2x + 6 newspapers in a week.
We know the hotel pays $4 for each Sunday newspaper and $1 for each non-Sunday newspaper.
So, the hotel pays 4(2x) + 1(7 - 1 - 2x) = 8x + 3 dollars for newspapers each week.
We know the hotel pays $210 per week for newspapers.
So, 8x + 3 = 210.
Solving for x, we get x = 26.25.
Since the hotel can only order whole numbers of newspapers, the hotel orders 26 newspapers on Monday.
The answer is therefore A: 15.

  Simplifying the equation, we get: 9y = 198
  Solving for y, we get: y = 22
  Therefore, the hotel buys 22 newspapers on Monday.
  The answer is A: 15.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 80 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y.
Choices:
  A: 144km
  B: 72 km
  C: 126km
  D: 84 km
  E: 48km
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let's assume the distance between X and Y is d km.
  Let's assume they meet for the second time at a distance of x km from X (and d-x km from Y).
  Let's calculate the time taken by Allen to reach Y and return to x.
  The time taken by Allen to reach Y = d/54.
  The time taken by Allen to reach x from Y = x/54.
  Therefore, the total time taken by Allen = d/54 + x/54.
  Let's calculate the time taken by Bob to reach X and return to (d-x).
  The time taken by Bob to reach X = d/78.
  The time taken by Bob to reach (d-x) from X = (d-x)/78.
  Therefore, the total time taken by Bob = d/78 + (d-x)/78.
  We know that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen when they meet for the second time.
  Therefore, (d-x)+48 = (d-x) * (78/54).
  Solving this equation, we get x = d/3.
  Substituting x = d/3 in the above equation, we get d = 126 km.
  Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 126 km.
  The answer is C: 126 km.
Action: Answer("C")

Thought:

  The time it takes for Allen to travel (d - x) km at 54 kmph is (d - x) / 54.
  The time it takes for Bob to travel x km at 78 kmph is x / 78.
  Since they start at the same time, the time it takes for them to meet for the first time is the same for both of them.
  Therefore, we have the equation: (d - x) / 54 = x / 78.
  Solving for x, we get x = 78d / 132.

  Allen travels a total distance of 2(d - x) km.
  Bob travels a total distance of 2x + 48 km.
  Since they both travel for the same amount of time, we can set up the equation: 2(d - x) / 54 = (2x + 48) / 78.
  Solving for d, we get d = 126 km.
  Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 126 km.

  We need to find the value of 'x' to calculate the total distance travelled.
  We can use the formula distance = speed × time.

Calculation:
  In the forward journey, the jeep travelled a distance of 6x km in 6 hours, so the speed was x km/hr.
  In the return journey, the jeep travelled the same distance in 4 hours, so the speed was (6x/4) = (3/2)x km/hr.
  Given that the speed in the return journey was increased by 12km/hr, we can write the following equation:
  (3/2)x + 12 = x
  Solving for x, we get x = 24 km/hr.
  Therefore, the total distance travelled by the jeep is 10x + 48 = 10(24) + 48 = 240 + 48 = 288 km.

Question: The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 28
  C: 30
  D: 53
  E: 59
Response 0:
Thought:
  If the number of water lilies doubles every two days, then the number of water lilies after n days is 2^(n/2).
  If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies.
  Therefore, 2^(60/2) = 2^30 = the number of water lilies after 60 days, when initially there was one water lily.
  If initially there were 64 water lilies, then the number of water lilies after n days is 64 * 2^(n/2).
  We need to find the number of days n such that 64 * 2^(n/2) = 2^30.
  Dividing both sides by 64, we get 2^(n/2) = 2^26.
  Therefore, n/2 = 26, and n = 52.
  The lake will be fully covered with lilies in 52 days.
  The answer is D: 53.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The number of water lilies doubles every two days.
  If there is one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with lilies.
  We need to find how many days it will take for a lake with 64 water lilies to be fully covered.
  We can use the formula N = N0 * 2^(t/k), where N0 is the initial number of lilies, N is the final number of lilies, t is the time elapsed, and k is the doubling time (2 days).
  We need to solve for t when N = 2^k.
  We can rewrite the formula as log2(N/N0) = t/k.
  Substituting N = 2^k and N0 = 64, we get log2(2^k/64) = t/2.
  Simplifying, we get k - 6 = t/2.
  Therefore, t = 2k - 12.
  If initially there were 64 water lilies, then N0 = 64.

  Taking the logarithm base 2 of both sides, we get k-6 = t/2k.
  Therefore, t = 2k - 12.

  Therefore, k = 33.
  Substituting k = 33 in t = 2k - 12, we get t = 54.
  Therefore, if initially there were 64 water lilies on the lake, it will take 54 days for the lake to be fully covered with lilies.

Question: A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another?
Choices:
  A: 1 hr 23 min
  B: 1 hr 15 min
  C: 1 hr 8 min
  D: 56 min
  E: 55 min
Response 0:
Thought:
  Train M travels for a total of 4 hours (5 am to 9 am).
  Train N travels for a total of 3.5 hours (7 am to 10:30 am).
  Let's assume that the two trains meet at time t hours after Train N leaves City B.
  In that case, Train M has traveled for t hours and Train N has traveled for (t-2) hours.
  The distance traveled by both trains when they meet is the same.
  Therefore, we can write the equation: 
  Distance traveled by Train M = Distance traveled by Train N
  Speed of Train M * t = Speed of Train N * (t-2)
  We know that the speed of Train M is greater than the speed of Train N, 
  so Train M will travel a greater distance than Train N in the same amount of time.
  Therefore, we can conclude that t < 4.
  Solving the equation, we get t = 7/3 hours = 2 hours and 20 minutes.
  Therefore, the two trains cross each other 2 hours and 20 minutes after Train N leaves City B, 
  which is at 9:20 am.
  The answer is not among the choices given. The closest answer is E: 55 min.

  The distance traveled by Train M in 2 hours is (d) because it travels for 4 hours in total.
  The distance traveled by Train N in 2 hours is (d) because it travels for 3.5 hours in total.
  The total distance traveled by both trains in 2 hours is (2d).
  The relative speed of the two trains is the sum of their speeds, which is the distance traveled divided by the time taken, or (2d) / 2 = d.
  We know that Train M travels at a speed of (d/4) and Train N travels at a speed of (d/3.5).
  Therefore, d = (d/4) + (d/3.5).

  The time taken by Train N to travel the remaining distance is (56 - d) / (d/3.5) = 1 hour and 15 minutes.
  Therefore, the two trains cross each other at 8:15 am.

  The relative speed of the two trains is the sum of their speeds.

  For Train N, Distance = Speed x Time = Speed_N x 3.5 hours
  Adding the two distances, we get Distance = Speed_M x 4 hours + Speed_N x 3.5 hours
  At the time the two trains meet, the total time taken by both trains is the same.

  Distance = Speed_M x t = Speed_N x (t - 2)
  Solving for t, we get t = 8/3 hours, or 2 hours and 40 minutes.
  The trains meet 2 hours and 40 minutes after Train M leaves City A, or at 7:40 am.
  Therefore, the answer is not one of the given choices.

  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8

  The total weight of the 11 vehicles is 11 * 14.8 = 162.8 tons.
  The total weight of the original 10 vehicles plus the weight of the new truck is 122 + x.

  Solving for x, we get x = 41.6.
  Therefore, the weight of the heavy duty truck is 41.6 tons.

Question: 10kg of a mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay. In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand how much of the mixture is to be removed and replaced with pure sand?
Choices:
  A: 10/7
  B: 20/7
  C: 30/7
  D: 40/7
  E: 50/7
Response 0:
Thought:
- The current mixture is 30% sand and 70% clay, which means there are 3kg of sand and 7kg of clay in the mixture.
- We want to make the mixture contain equal quantities of sand and clay. Let's assume we need to remove x kg of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.
- After we remove x kg of the mixture, we will have (10-x) kg of the mixture left. Since we want the mixture to contain equal quantities of sand and clay, we need to have (10-x)/2 kg of sand and (10-x)/2 kg of clay.
- We will remove x kg of the mixture, which contains 0.3x kg of sand and 0.7x kg of clay.
- We will add x kg of pure sand, so the final mixture will contain 3+0.7x kg of clay and 0.3x+ x = 1.3x kg of sand.
- We want the final mixture to contain equal quantities of sand and clay, so we need to have (10-x)/2 kg of sand and (10-x)/2 kg of clay.
- Setting the amount of clay equal and solving for x, we get:
```
3 + 0.7x = (10-x)/2
6 + 1.4x = 10 - x
2.4x = 4
x = 10/6 = 5/3
```
- Therefore, we need to remove 5/3 kg of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.
- Checking the answer, we can verify that the final mixture will contain 4kg of sand and 4kg of clay.
Action: Answer("A")

Response 9:
Thought:
Let us assume that the initial quantity of sand in the mixture is x kg.
So, the initial quantity of clay in the mixture is (10 - x) kg.

The mixture is 30% sand and 70% clay.
This means that the weight of sand in the mixture is 0.3*10 = 3 kg.
And, the weight of clay in the mixture is 0.7*10 = 7 kg.

In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand, we need to remove some of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.
Let us assume that we need to remove y kg of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.

After removing y kg of the mixture, the weight of sand in the mixture will still be x kg.
And, the weight of clay in the mixture will be (10 - x - y) kg.

Now, we need to add y kg of pure sand to the mixture.
So, the weight of sand in the final mixture will be (x + y) kg.
And, the weight of clay in the final mixture will still be (10 - x - y) kg.

We want the weight of sand and clay to be equal in the final mixture.
Therefore, we can write the equation:
x + y = 10 - x - y
=> 2y = 10 - x - x
=> 2y = 10 - 2x
=> y = (10 - 2x)/2
=> y = 5 - x

We need to find the value of y such that the weight of the mixture removed is equal to the weight of pure sand added.
The weight of the mixture removed is y kg.
The weight of pure sand added is 0.3*y kg.

Therefore, we can write the equation:
y = 0.3*y
=> 0.7*y = 0
=> y = 0

This means that we do not need to remove any mixture to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand.
We can simply add pure sand to the mixture.

The weight of sand in the final mixture will be half of the total weight of the mixture.
Therefore, the weight of pure sand that needs to be added to the mixture is:
0.5*(10) - 3 = 2 kg

Question: Find the total no. of distinct bike no.'s that can beformed using 2 letters followed by 2 no.'s. How many letters need to be distinct?
Choices:
  A: 74453
  B: 64543
  C: 74325
  D: 65000
  E: 97656
Response 0:
Thought:
  We need to find the total number of distinct bike numbers that can be formed using 2 letters followed by 2 numbers.
  There are 26 letters in the English alphabet.
  There are 10 digits (0-9).
  The total number of ways to choose 2 letters from 26 letters is 26C2 = (26*25)/(2*1) = 325
  The total number of ways to choose 2 digits from 10 digits is 10C2 = (10*9)/(2*1) = 45
  The number of distinct bike numbers that can be formed is the product of the number of ways to choose 2 letters and the number of ways to choose 2 digits.
  Therefore, the total number of distinct bike numbers that can be formed using 2 letters followed by 2 no.'s is 325*45 = 14625.
  The number of letters that need to be distinct is 2.

Question: If Jill needed to buy 10 bottles of soda for a party in which 8 people attended, how many bottles of soda will she need to buy for a party in which 12 people are attending?
Choices:
  A: 6
  B: 8
  C: 10
  D: 12
  E: 14
Response 0:
Thought:
  Jill needed 10 bottles of soda for a party of 8 people.
  This means that each person consumed 10/8 = 1.25 bottles of soda.
  To find out how many bottles of soda Jill needs for a party of 12 people, we can use the same ratio.
  Jill will need 1.25 x 12 = 15 bottles of soda.
  Therefore, the answer is E: 14.
Action: Answer("E")

  To solve for x, we can cross-multiply and simplify: 8x = 120, x = 15.
  Therefore, Jill will need to buy 15 bottles of soda for a party in which 12 people are attending.

Question: What will be the cost of gardening 1-metre – broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre?
Choices:
  A: 3400
  B: 1700
  C: 3440
  D: Cannot be determined
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Thought:
  A rectangular plot with perimeter 340 meters has sides that add up to 170 meters.
  Let's say one side of the rectangular plot is x meters. Then the other side is (170 - x) meters.
  A 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot would increase both sides by 2 meters.
  The area of the 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot is (x+2)*(170-x+2) - x*(170-x).
  Simplifying the expression gives 172x - 2x^2 + 344.
  The area of the 1-meter broad boundary is 172x - 2x^2 + 344 square meters.
  At the rate of 10 per square meter, the cost of gardening 1 square meter is 10.
  Therefore, the cost of gardening the 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot is (172x - 2x^2 + 344) * 10.
  We need to find the value of x to calculate the cost.
  We know that the perimeter of the rectangular plot is 340 meters.
  2(x + 170 - x) = 340
  2 * 170 = 340
  Therefore, the perimeter of the rectangular plot is 2 * (x + 170 - x) = 340 meters.
  The answer can be calculated using this information.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's consider the rectangular plot has length L and breadth B.
  The perimeter of the plot is given as 340 metres.
  Therefore, 2(L+B) = 340
  L+B = 170
  We need to find the cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot.
  The length and breadth of the plot after gardening will be L+2 and B+2 respectively.
  The area of the gardening will be (L+2)(B+2) - LB
  The cost of gardening will be the area of gardening multiplied by the rate per square meter.
  Therefore, the cost of gardening will be (L+2)(B+2) - LB x 10
  
  As we don't have the values of L and B, we cannot determine the exact cost of gardening. However, we can calculate the cost of gardening for some arbitrary values of L and B.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Cannot be determined. 
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Let's first find the length and width of the rectangular plot.
  Let L be the length and W be the width.
  We know that the perimeter of a rectangle is P = 2L + 2W = 340 meters.
  We can simplify this to L + W = 170 meters.
  We also know that we need to garden a 1-meter boundary around the rectangular plot.
  Therefore, the new dimensions of the plot will be (L + 2) meters by (W + 2) meters.
  The area of the boundary will be (L + 2)(W + 2) - LW square meters.
  The cost of gardening will be 10 times the area of the boundary.
  We can simplify the expression for the cost of gardening to 10(2L + 2W + 4) square meters.
  Substituting L + W = 170, we get the cost of gardening to be 10(2(170) + 4) = 3440.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 3440.

  L + W = 170

  The area of the rectangular plot will be L * W.
  The area of the boundary will be the difference between the area of the rectangular plot including the boundary and the area of the rectangular plot.
  Area of the boundary = (L + 2) * (W + 2) - L * W
  Area of the boundary = LW + 2L + 2W + 4 - LW
  Area of the boundary = 2L + 2W + 4
  Cost of gardening the boundary will be the area of the boundary multiplied by the rate of 10 per square metre.
  Cost of gardening the boundary = (2L + 2W + 4) * 10
  Cost of gardening the boundary = 20L + 20W + 40
  We have two equations: L + W = 170 and Cost of gardening the boundary = 20L + 20W + 40.
  We can use these equations to solve for L and W and find the cost of gardening the boundary.
  Let's solve for L and W:
  L = 170 - W
  Cost of gardening the boundary = 20(170 - W) + 20W + 40
  Cost of gardening the boundary = 3400 + 20W - 20W + 40
  Cost of gardening the boundary = 3440
  Therefore, the cost of gardening 1-metre broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre will be 3440.
  The answer is C: 3440.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 90 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the percentage gain of a merchant who purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450 and sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg.
Choices:
  A: 50 %
  B: 60 %
  C: 55 %
  D: 70 %
  E: 58%
Response 0:
Thought:
  The cost price of 1 kg of orange is 450/90 = Rs. 5
  The selling price of 1 kg of orange is Rs. 7.50
  The profit made on 1 kg of orange is Rs. 7.50 - Rs. 5 = Rs. 2.50
  The profit percentage can be calculated as (Profit/Cost Price) * 100
  Therefore, the profit percentage in this case is (2.5/5) * 100 = 50%
  The answer is A: 50%
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The cost price of 1 kg of oranges = 450/90 = 5 Rs.
  The selling price of 1 kg of oranges = 7.50 Rs.
  Profit per kg of oranges = 7.50 - 5 = 2.50 Rs.
  Profit percentage = (Profit / Cost Price) x 100%
  Profit percentage = (2.50 / 5) x 100%
  Profit percentage = 50%
  Therefore, the percentage gain of the merchant is 50%.
Action: Answer("A")

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joe’s fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?
Choices:
  A: 45
  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume:
  Joe's age = J
  Joe's sister's age = S
  Joe's father's age = F

  From the first statement, we know:
  J + S + F = 100

  From the second statement, we know:
  J + (F - J) = F
  F - J = J
  F = 2J

  Substituting the value of F in the first equation:
  J + S + 2J = 100
  3J + S = 100

  From the third statement, we know:
  J + (F - S) = 2(S - F)
  J + 2J - S = 2S - 4J
  3J - S = 2S - 4J
  7J = 3S

  We can substitute this value of S in the equation 3J + S = 100 to get the value of J:
  7J = 300
  J = 43

  We can now use the value of J to calculate F:
  F = 2J
  F = 2 * 43
  F = 86

  Therefore, the age of Joe's father is 86.
  The answer is E: 58.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume Joe's age is "j", Joe's sister's age is "s", and Joe's father's age is "f".
  From the first statement, we know that j + s + f = 100.
  Let's assume that when Joe is as old as his father, their age will be "x".
  Then, we can write an equation: x = j + (x - f)
  Simplifying the equation, we get f = (j + s)/2.
  Now, let's assume that when Joe is as old as his father, his sister's age will be "y".
  Then, we can write another equation: y = 2s - (x - j) = 2s - (f + s) = s - f.
  Simplifying the equation, we get f = (s - y)/2.
  Equating both expressions of f, we get (j + s)/2 = (s - y)/2.
  Simplifying the equation, we get j = y.
  Substituting j = y in the first equation, we get s + 2j = 100.
  We also know that f = (j + s)/2.
  Solving these two equations, we get f = 48.
  Therefore, the age of Joe's father is 48.
  The answer is B: 48.

    j + f = 2(s)

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Thought:
  Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan every time the coin lands on Heads.
  Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher every time the coin lands on Tails.
  Let's assume the coin landed on Heads x times and Tails y times.
  Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan x times.
  Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher y times.
  The total amount Christopher gives to Jonathan is $2x.
  The total amount Jonathan gives to Christopher is $3y.
  The total amount Christopher and Jonathan exchange is $2x - $3y.
  Since they neither won nor lost any amount, $2x = $3y.
  Therefore, x/y = 3/2.
  We know that x + y = 20.
  Solving these equations, we get x = 12 and y = 8.
  Therefore, the coin landed on Heads 12 times.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought:
  If Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan each time it turns heads and Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher each time it turns tails, then the net amount exchanged during each flip is $1 from Jonathan to Christopher.
  If there was no net gain or loss, then the number of times the coin landed on heads must be equal to the number of times it landed on tails.
  The total number of flips was 20, so the number of times the coin landed on heads and tails must each be 10.

  2x = 3y

Topic: Math
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's suppose the distance between A and B be "d".
  Let's also suppose that Kevin took "t" hours to reach B from A.
  Therefore, Kevin took "2t" hours to travel from B back to A.
  Using the formula distance = speed x time, we can write the following equations:
    d = 70t  (distance from A to B)
    d = 90(2t-3) + 70  (distance from B to A, 3 hours before the end of the trip)
  We can solve for "t" by equating the two equations:
    70t = 90(2t-3) + 70
    70t = 180t - 240
    t = 3
  Substituting "t=3" in the first equation, we can find "d":
    d = 70t = 70 x 3 = 210
  Therefore, the distance between A and B is 210 miles.
  The answer is E: None of the above.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the distance between A and B is "d".
  Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph, which means the time he took is d/70.
  Kevin turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph, which means the time he took is d/90.
  Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it, which means he had traveled a total of d-70 miles.
  Let's assume that the time left is "t". Therefore, the time he traveled so far is d/70 + d/90 + t.
  We can set up an equation: d/70 + d/90 + t = (d-70)/90.
  We can simplify the equation to: 9d + 7d = 12600 + 630t.
  We can simplify further to: d = 1800 + 90t.
  Therefore, the distance between A and B is 1800 miles.
  The answer is A: 180.

  We can set up an equation: 
  (x/70 + 0.25 + x/90 - 3) = (x - 70)/70
  Solving for x, we get x = 270.
  Therefore, the distance between A and B is 270 miles.

  d = rt => t = d/r = d/70
  After reaching B, Kevin turns around and comes back to A.

  We also know that he was 70 miles away from B at this time.

  d = rt => d = 90(t'+t-3)
  We also know that the total distance he covered is 2d.
  Therefore, we can use the formula d = rt, where r is the rate, to find the time it takes for Kevin to cover 2d at an average speed of (2d)/(t+t'-3).
  d = rt => t + t' = 2d/(t+t'-3)
  We have three equations and three variables (d, t, t'). We can solve for them using algebraic manipulation.

  Substituting t and t' in equation 2, we get d = 630

Question: I know a 5 digit number having a property that with a 1 after it, it is three times as large as it would be with a 1 before it.
What is that number?
Choices:
  A: 42857
  B: 32456
  C: 76523
  D: 24567
  E: 43566
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the 5-digit number be 'abcde'.
  With a 1 after it, the new number will be 'abcde1'.
  With a 1 before it, the new number will be '1abcde'.
  According to the problem statement, the following equation is true:
  3*(1abcde) = abcde1
  Therefore, 
  3*(10000a + 1000b + 100c + 10d + e) = 100000a + 10000b + 1000c + 100d + 10e + 1
  29999a = 999b + 199c + 29d + 3e + 1
  a can only be 1, 2, 3, 4, or 5. Let's try each of them.
  If a=1, then 29999 = 999b + 199c + 29d + 3e + 1, but the right-hand side is not divisible by 3, so a cannot be 1.
  If a=2, then 59998 = 999b + 199c + 29d + 3e + 1. By trial and error, we can find that b=4, c=2, d=8, and e=5 satisfy the equation.
  Therefore, the 5-digit number is 42,857.
  The answer is A: 42857.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume there are 'n' employees in the organization.
  If each employee contributes equally, then the amount contributed by each employee is Rs. (600000/n).
  If each employee contributes Rs. 60 extra, then the amount contributed by each employee is Rs. ((600000+6000)/n) = Rs. (612000/n).
  According to the problem, (600000/n) + 60 = (612000/n).
  Solving the above equation, we get n = 400.
  Therefore, there are 400 employees in that organization.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume the number of employees in the organization is "x".
  Each employee contributes the same amount, so the total contribution is equal to the number of employees times the amount contributed by each employee.
  Let "y" be the amount contributed by each employee.
  Then, we know that xy = 6,00,000 (Rs. 6 lakh).
  If each employee had contributed Rs. 60 more, then the new amount contributed by each employee would be y+60.
  The new total contribution would be x(y+60) = 6,24,000 (Rs. 6.24 lakh).
  We can simplify this equation to xy + 60x = 6,24,000.
  Substituting xy = 6,00,000, we get 6,00,000 + 60x = 6,24,000.
  Solving for x, we get x = 400.
  Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Let's assume that there are n employees in the organization.
  If each employee contributes x amount, then the total contribution would be n*x.
  The total contribution is Rs. 6 lakh, so we have n*x = 6,00,000.
  If each employee contributes Rs. 60 extra, then the new contribution from each employee would be (x+60).
  The total contribution with the increased amount is Rs. 6.24 lakh, so we have n*(x+60) = 6,24,000.
  We can simplify the two equations to get x = 600/n and x+60 = 624/n.
  We can solve for n by equating the two expressions for x.
  Therefore, 600/n + 60 = 624/n, which simplifies to n = 200.
  Therefore, there are 200 employees in the organization.
  The answer is B: 200.

Topic: Math
Question: A man divides Rs 8600 among 5 sons, 4 daughters and 2 nephews. If each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, and each son receives five as much as each nephew. How much does each daughter receive ?
Choices:
  A: Rs 400
  B: Rs 500
  C: Rs 600
  D: Rs 700
  E: Rs 800
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let the amount received by each nephew be x.

Question: A student instead of finding the value of 7/8 of a number, found the value of 7/18 of the number. If his answer differed from the actual one by 770, find the that number.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 2520
  C: 1728
  D: 1656
  E: None
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the number is "x".
  According to the problem, the student found the value of 7/18 of the number, which is (7/18)x.
  The student should have found the value of 7/8 of the number, which is (7/8)x.
  We know that the difference between the two values is 770, so we can write an equation:
  (7/8)x - (7/18)x = 770
  Solving for x:
  (77/72)x = 770
  x = (72/77) * 770
  x = 720
  Therefore, the number is 720.
  The answer is E: None of the above.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's say the actual number is x.
  The student found 7/18 of the number, which is (7/18)x.
  The student should have found 7/8 of the number, which is (7/8)x.
  The student's answer differed from the actual one by 770, which means (7/8)x - (7/18)x = 770.
  Simplifying the equation, we get (35/72)x = 770.
  Solving for x, we get x = (770*72)/35 = 1584.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 1584.

Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the maximum distance you can travel with $8.50 on a cab which charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
Choices:
  A: 11.75 miles
  B: 12.75 miles
  C: 17.75 miles
  D: 14.75 miles
  E: 10.75 miles
Response 0:
Thought:
  The cab charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and $0.10 for each additional quarter mile.
  Let's calculate the maximum distance that can be traveled with the given amount.
  $8.50 - $3.50 = $5.00 is the amount left to spend on additional quarter miles.
  Each additional quarter mile costs $0.10.
  Therefore, the maximum distance that can be traveled is $5.00 / $0.10 = 50 quarter miles.
  One mile is equal to 4 quarter miles.
  Therefore, the maximum distance in miles is 50 / 4 = 12.5 miles.
  The answer is closest to 12.75 miles, which is choice B.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The cab charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile. That means the remaining $5.00 will be used for the additional distance.
  The additional distance costs 10 cents per quarter-mile.
  We can find the maximum distance by dividing the remaining $5.00 by 0.10.
  $5.00 ÷ $0.10 = 50 quarter-miles.
  The total distance is the sum of the first quarter-mile and 50 quarter-miles.
  Total distance = 1 + 50/4 = 13 miles.
  Therefore, the maximum distance you can travel with $8.50 is 13 miles.
